## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws express dA/dt as power-law or rational functions of A, with possible time-dependent terms for non-autonomous systems (e.g., catalyst deactivation, photochemistry, or periodic forcing).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate)
- Mixed-order / Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (surface-catalyzed reaction with saturation)
- Second-order Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (bimolecular surface reaction)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or activation over time)
- Photochemical with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (linearly time-varying external influence)
- Power-law with time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics substrate consumption)
- Competitive inhibition form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Catalyst deactivation: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (sum of decaying and persistent catalytic pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no t) → classical autonomous rate law; presence of t suggests non-autonomous effects like catalyst aging or external forcing
- Rational functions of A (A/(K+A)) → enzyme or surface saturation kinetics where active sites become limiting
- Product form A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or logistic kinetics where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Negative rate constants → consumption/decay of reactant; positive constants with A terms → production or autocatalysis
- Exponential dependence on t (exp(c*t)) → catalyst deactivation, temperature ramping, or time-varying external conditions
- Fractional power of A (A**c with 0<c<1) → fractal kinetics or diffusion-limited reactions in heterogeneous media
- Sum of terms with different A-powers → parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Denominator polynomials in A → competitive adsorption or multiple binding site mechanisms
